,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"\r\n## TL;DR\r\nYou asked: \"How do I serve a Section 21 notice correctly
in England?\". In England, possession usually starts with the right notice and clean compliance records. If you have a
straightforward nofault route, a Section 21 notice (Form 6A) can be right, but only if the tenancy is an AST and you
have complied with deposit protection, prescribed information, EPC, gas safety, and How to Rent requirements. If the
tenant has breached the tenancy (rent arrears or other grounds), a Section 8 notice (Form 3) may be the correct route.
Use the free tools to sensecheck before you serve anything: [Free Section 21 generator](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/to
ols/free-section-21-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content
=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england), [Free Section 8 generator](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/free-section-8-
notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-sectio
n-21-notice-england), and the [Free eviction notice checker](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/validators?utm_source=a
sk_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england). When
you need a full court bundle for England, the [Complete eviction pack](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/products/complete-p
ack?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-e
ngland) keeps everything consistent. If you want a guided flow, start with the [noticeonly wizard](https://landlordheav
en.co.uk/wizard?product=notice_only\u0026src=product_page\u0026topic=eviction\u0026utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_mediu
m=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england). You can always [Ask a followup
in Ask Heaven](/ask-heaven).\r\n\r\n## What the law generally says\r\nPossession in England is a legal process. You
cannot change locks, remove belongings, or pressure a tenant to leave without a court order. Notices must be valid and
served correctly, and the court will dismiss or delay cases when compliance is missing or the notice period is wrong.
A Section 21 claim is usually “accelerated” (N5B) if it is genuinely nofault and no rent arrears are claimed in the
same action. A Section 8 claim is “standard” possession and requires you to prove the ground(s). Both routes require
documentary evidence such as the tenancy agreement, deposit compliance certificate, prescribed information, gas safety
records, and EPCs. Always keep a clear paper trail. For practical comparisons, see [Section 21 validity checklist
(Form 6A)](/ask-heaven/section-21-validity-checklist-form-6a) and [Section 8 Ground 8 mandatory
arrears](/ask-heaven/section-8-ground-8-mandatory-arrears).\r\n\r\n## Englandspecific notes (AST, Section 21, Section
8)\r\nEngland uses assured shorthold tenancy (AST) terminology. Section 21 is served on Form 6A and is the usual no
fault route when the tenancy is periodic or a fixed term has ended. Section 8 is served on Form 3 and relies on
specific grounds. Common grounds include Ground 8 (mandatory rent arrears), Ground 10 (some arrears), Ground 11
(persistent late payment), and discretionary grounds like nuisance or damage. If your facts depend on evidence (rent
schedule, tenancy clauses, complaint logs), prepare those early. If the tenant defends the claim, a hearing may be
required even for Section 21. For court timing, see [accelerated possession
timetable](/ask-heaven/accelerated-possession-timetable-england).\r\n\r\n## What to do next (stepbystep)\r\n1.
Identify the correct route. Use Section 21 for nofault if your compliance is clean. Use Section 8 if a breach exists
and you want to rely on grounds. If you are unsure, begin with the [noticeonly wizard](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/wiz
ard?product=notice_only\u0026src=product_page\u0026topic=eviction\u0026utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026u
tm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england).\r\n2. Review compliance documents: deposit
protection, prescribed information, EPC, gas safety, and How to Rent. Fix gaps before serving a Section 21.\r\n3.
Build a clear rent schedule if you are claiming arrears. This helps with Ground 8 and later money claims.\r\n4. Choose
the right form: Form 6A for Section 21, Form 3 for Section 8. If you are at all unsure, generate a draft with the free
tools.\r\n5. Serve the notice correctly: follow the service clause in the AST, keep proof of posting or delivery, and
record the date.\r\n6. Diary the expiry date and prepare your court bundle early. If you need a straightforward
Section 21 court route, prepare N5B.\r\n7. If no possession is obtained after the notice, file the claim promptly to
avoid timing issues.\r\n8. At every stage, keep a clear paper trail and keep communication professional.\r\n\r\n##
Common mistakes\r\n- Serving Section 21 without valid deposit protection or prescribed information.\r\n- Using the
wrong form or notice period.\r\n- Mixing Section 21 and Section 8 evidence without clarity on the primary route.\r\n-
Failing to keep a rent schedule or proof of service.\r\n- Relying on informal communications instead of formal
notices.\r\n- Missing gas safety or EPC service dates and then trying to backfill.\r\n- Not checking that the tenancy
is an AST and that the notice is signed and dated correctly.\r\n- Ignoring the possibility of a tenant defense or a
disrepair counterclaim.\r\n\r\n## What happens if you get it wrong\r\nInvalid notices waste time and money, and the
court may dismiss your claim. You might have to reserve a notice and wait out a new notice period. A poor paper trail
can also create risks if the tenant raises issues such as disrepair, deposit noncompliance, or retaliatory eviction.
In some cases, failing to follow the correct legal steps could expose you to claims of unlawful eviction or
harassment. That is why it is worth sensechecking the notice with the [Free eviction notice checker](https://landlordhe
aven.co.uk/tools/validators?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-s
erve-section-21-notice-england) before you serve.\r\n\r\n## Next steps + tools/templates\r\n- Start with the guided
[noticeonly wizard](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/wizard?product=notice_only\u0026src=product_page\u0026topic=eviction\u

ngland) if you want the flow to ask you the right questions.\r\n- Draft the correct notice: [Free Section 21 generator]
(https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/free-section-21-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm

oducts/ast?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-n
otice-england).\r\n- For related guidance, see [Section 21 validity

costs](/ask-heaven/accelerated-possession-costs-fees).\r\n- Ask followups in the hub: [Ask a followup in Ask
Heaven](/ask-heaven).\r\n\r\n## Evidence checklist (England)\r\nBefore serving or issuing a claim, make sure you can
produce the following if asked by a court:\r\n- A signed AST or clear evidence of the tenancy terms.\r\n- Deposit
protection certificate and prescribed information service proof.\r\n- Current EPC and proof it was given to the
tenant.\r\n- Gas safety certificates covering the tenancy period.\r\n- How to Rent guide service evidence (if
required).\r\n- A rent schedule showing payments and arrears.\r\n- Proof of notice service (postal receipt, witness
statement, or signed acknowledgment).\r\n- Any communications relevant to breaches or arrears.\r\n\r\n##
Disclaimer\r\nThis answer is general information for England and is not legal advice. It does not replace advice from
a solicitor or qualified adviser. If you are unsure about your specific circumstances, seek legal advice before

asked: \"How do I serve a Section 21 notice correctly in England?\". In England, possession usually starts with the
right notice and clean compliance records. If you have a straightforward nofault route, a Section 21 notice (Form 6A)
can be right, but only if the tenancy is an AST and you have complied with deposit protection, prescribed information,
EPC, gas safety, and How to Rent requirements. If the tenant has breached the tenancy (rent arrears or other grounds),
a Section 8 notice (Form 3) may be the correct route. Use the free tools to sensecheck before you serve anything:
[Free Section 21 generator](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/free-section-21-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven\u
0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england), [Free Section 8 ge
nerator](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/free-section-8-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u
0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england), and the [Free eviction notice checker]
(https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/validators?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026u
tm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england). When you need a full court bundle for England, the [Complete
eviction pack](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/products/complete-pack?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_c
ampaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england) keeps everything consistent. If you want a
guided flow, start with the [noticeonly wizard](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/wizard?product=notice_only\u0026src=produc
t_page\u0026topic=eviction\u0026utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-
to-serve-section-21-notice-england). You can always [Ask a followup in Ask Heaven](/ask-heaven).\r\n\r\n## What the
law generally says\r\nPossession in England is a legal process. You cannot change locks, remove belongings, or
pressure a tenant to leave without a court order. Notices must be valid and served correctly, and the court will
dismiss or delay cases when compliance is missing or the notice period is wrong. A Section 21 claim is usually
“accelerated” (N5B) if it is genuinely nofault and no rent arrears are claimed in the same action. A Section 8 claim
is “standard” possession and requires you to prove the ground(s). Both routes require documentary evidence such as the
tenancy agreement, deposit compliance certificate, prescribed information, gas safety records, and EPCs. Always keep a
clear paper trail. For practical comparisons, see [Section 21 validity checklist (Form
6A)](/ask-heaven/section-21-validity-checklist-form-6a) and [Section 8 Ground 8 mandatory
arrears](/ask-heaven/section-8-ground-8-mandatory-arrears).\r\n\r\n## Englandspecific notes (AST, Section 21, Section
8)\r\nEngland uses assured shorthold tenancy (AST) terminology. Section 21 is served on Form 6A and is the usual no
fault route when the tenancy is periodic or a fixed term has ended. Section 8 is served on Form 3 and relies on
specific grounds. Common grounds include Ground 8 (mandatory rent arrears), Ground 10 (some arrears), Ground 11
(persistent late payment), and discretionary grounds like nuisance or damage. If your facts depend on evidence (rent
schedule, tenancy clauses, complaint logs), prepare those early. If the tenant defends the claim, a hearing may be
required even for Section 21. For court timing, see [accelerated possession
timetable](/ask-heaven/accelerated-possession-timetable-england).\r\n\r\n## What to do next (stepbystep)\r\n1.
Identify the correct route. Use Section 21 for nofault if your compliance is clean. Use Section 8 if a breach exists
and you want to rely on grounds. If you are unsure, begin with the [noticeonly wizard](https://landlordheaven.co.uk/wiz
ard?product=notice_only\u0026src=product_page\u0026topic=eviction\u0026utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026u
tm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england).\r\n2. Review compliance documents: deposit
protection, prescribed information, EPC, gas safety, and How to Rent. Fix gaps before serving a Section 21.\r\n3.
Build a clear rent schedule if you are claiming arrears. This helps with Ground 8 and later money claims.\r\n4. Choose
the right form: Form 6A for Section 21, Form 3 for Section 8. If you are at all unsure, generate a draft with the free
tools.\r\n5. Serve the notice correctly: follow the service clause in the AST, keep proof of posting or delivery, and
record the date.\r\n6. Diary the expiry date and prepare your court bundle early. If you need a straightforward
Section 21 court route, prepare N5B.\r\n7. If no possession is obtained after the notice, file the claim promptly to
avoid timing issues.\r\n8. At every stage, keep a clear paper trail and keep communication professional.\r\n\r\n##
Common mistakes\r\n- Serving Section 21 without valid deposit protection or prescribed information.\r\n- Using the
wrong form or notice period.\r\n- Mixing Section 21 and Section 8 evidence without clarity on the primary route.\r\n-
Failing to keep a rent schedule or proof of service.\r\n- Relying on informal communications instead of formal
notices.\r\n- Missing gas safety or EPC service dates and then trying to backfill.\r\n- Not checking that the tenancy
is an AST and that the notice is signed and dated correctly.\r\n- Ignoring the possibility of a tenant defense or a
disrepair counterclaim.\r\n\r\n## What happens if you get it wrong\r\nInvalid notices waste time and money, and the
court may dismiss your claim. You might have to reserve a notice and wait out a new notice period. A poor paper trail
can also create risks if the tenant raises issues such as disrepair, deposit noncompliance, or retaliatory eviction.
In some cases, failing to follow the correct legal steps could expose you to claims of unlawful eviction or
harassment. That is why it is worth sensechecking the notice with the [Free eviction notice checker](https://landlordhe
aven.co.uk/tools/validators?utm_source=ask_heaven\u0026utm_medium=seo\u0026utm_campaign=pilot\u0026utm_content=how-to-s
erve-section-21-notice-england) before you serve.\r\n\r\n## Next steps + tools/templates\r\n- Start with the guided

ngland) if you want the flow to ask you the right questions.\r\n- Draft the correct notice: [Free Section 21 generator]

produce the following if asked by a court:\r\n- A signed AST or clear evidence of the tenancy terms.\r\n- Deposit
protection certificate and prescribed information service proof.\r\n- Current EPC and proof it was given to the
tenant.\r\n- Gas safety certificates covering the tenancy period.\r\n- How to Rent guide service evidence (if
required).\r\n- A rent schedule showing payments and arrears.\r\n- Proof of notice service (postal receipt, witness
statement, or signed acknowledgment).\r\n- Any communications relevant to breaches or arrears.\r\n\r\n##

class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">TL;DR</h2>
<p class="text-sm leading-relaxed text-gray-800 mb-2 last:mb-0">You asked: &quot;How do I serve a Section 21 notice
correctly in England?&quot;. In England, possession usually starts with the right notice and clean compliance records.
If you have a straightforward nofault route, a Section 21 notice (Form 6A) can be right, but only if the tenancy is an
AST and you have complied with deposit protection, prescribed information, EPC, gas safety, and How to Rent
requirements. If the tenant has breached the tenancy (rent arrears or other grounds), a Section 8 notice (Form 3) may
be the correct route. Use the free tools to sensecheck before you serve anything: <a href="https://landlordheaven.co.uk
/tools/free-section-21-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven&amp;utm_medium=seo&amp;utm_campaign=pilot&amp;utm_content

rel="noopener noreferrer" node="[object Object]">Free Section 21 generator</a>, <a href="https://landlordheaven.co.uk/t
ools/free-section-8-notice-generator?utm_source=ask_heaven&amp;utm_medium=seo&amp;utm_campaign=pilot&amp;utm_content=ho
w-to-serve-section-21-notice-england" class="text-primary underline underline-offset-2 break-words" target="_blank"

<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">What the law generally says</h2>
<p class="text-sm leading-relaxed text-gray-800 mb-2 last:mb-0">Possession in England is a legal process. You cannot
change locks, remove belongings, or pressure a tenant to leave without a court order. Notices must be valid and served
correctly, and the court will dismiss or delay cases when compliance is missing or the notice period is wrong. A
Section 21 claim is usually “accelerated” (N5B) if it is genuinely nofault and no rent arrears are claimed in the same
action. A Section 8 claim is “standard” possession and requires you to prove the ground(s). Both routes require
documentary evidence such as the tenancy agreement, deposit compliance certificate, prescribed information, gas safety
records, and EPCs. Always keep a clear paper trail. For practical comparisons, see <a
href="/ask-heaven/section-21-validity-checklist-form-6a" class="text-primary underline underline-offset-2 break-words"
node="[object Object]">Section 21 validity checklist (Form 6A)</a> and <a
href="/ask-heaven/section-8-ground-8-mandatory-arrears" class="text-primary underline underline-offset-2 break-words"
node="[object Object]">Section 8 Ground 8 mandatory arrears</a>.</p>
<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">England‑specific notes (AST, Section 21, Section 8)</h2>
<p class="text-sm leading-relaxed text-gray-800 mb-2 last:mb-0">England uses assured shorthold tenancy (AST)
terminology. Section 21 is served on Form 6A and is the usual nofault route when the tenancy is periodic or a fixed
term has ended. Section 8 is served on Form 3 and relies on specific grounds. Common grounds include Ground 8
(mandatory rent arrears), Ground 10 (some arrears), Ground 11 (persistent late payment), and discretionary grounds
like nuisance or damage. If your facts depend on evidence (rent schedule, tenancy clauses, complaint logs), prepare
those early. If the tenant defends the claim, a hearing may be required even for Section 21. For court timing, see <a
href="/ask-heaven/accelerated-possession-timetable-england" class="text-primary underline underline-offset-2
break-words" node="[object Object]">accelerated possession timetable</a>.</p>
<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">What to do next (step‑by‑step)</h2>
<ol class="list-decimal pl-5 space-y-1 my-2 text-sm text-gray-800">
<li class="leading-relaxed">Identify the correct route. Use Section 21 for nofault if your compliance is clean. Use
Section 8 if a breach exists and you want to rely on grounds. If you are unsure, begin with the <a href="https://landlo
rdheaven.co.uk/wizard?product=notice_only&amp;src=product_page&amp;topic=eviction&amp;utm_source=ask_heaven&amp;utm_med
ium=seo&amp;utm_campaign=pilot&amp;utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england" class="text-primary underline
underline-offset-2 break-words" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" node="[object Object]">noticeonly
wizard</a>.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Review compliance documents: deposit protection, prescribed information, EPC, gas safety,
and How to Rent. Fix gaps before serving a Section 21.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Build a clear rent schedule if you are claiming arrears. This helps with Ground 8 and
later money claims.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Choose the right form: Form 6A for Section 21, Form 3 for Section 8. If you are at all
unsure, generate a draft with the free tools.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Serve the notice correctly: follow the service clause in the AST, keep proof of posting or
delivery, and record the date.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Diary the expiry date and prepare your court bundle early. If you need a straightforward
Section 21 court route, prepare N5B.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">If no possession is obtained after the notice, file the claim promptly to avoid timing
issues.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">At every stage, keep a clear paper trail and keep communication professional.</li>
</ol>
<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">Common mistakes</h2>
<ul class="list-disc pl-5 space-y-1 my-2 text-sm text-gray-800">
<li class="leading-relaxed">Serving Section 21 without valid deposit protection or prescribed information.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Using the wrong form or notice period.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Mixing Section 21 and Section 8 evidence without clarity on the primary route.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Failing to keep a rent schedule or proof of service.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Relying on informal communications instead of formal notices.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Missing gas safety or EPC service dates and then trying to back‑fill.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Not checking that the tenancy is an AST and that the notice is signed and dated
correctly.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Ignoring the possibility of a tenant defense or a disrepair counterclaim.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">What happens if you get it wrong</h2>
<p class="text-sm leading-relaxed text-gray-800 mb-2 last:mb-0">Invalid notices waste time and money, and the court
may dismiss your claim. You might have to reserve a notice and wait out a new notice period. A poor paper trail can
also create risks if the tenant raises issues such as disrepair, deposit noncompliance, or retaliatory eviction. In
some cases, failing to follow the correct legal steps could expose you to claims of unlawful eviction or harassment.
That is why it is worth sensechecking the notice with the <a href="https://landlordheaven.co.uk/tools/validators?utm_so
urce=ask_heaven&amp;utm_medium=seo&amp;utm_campaign=pilot&amp;utm_content=how-to-serve-section-21-notice-england"
class="text-primary underline underline-offset-2 break-words" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" node="[object
Object]">Free eviction notice checker</a> before you serve.</p>

<h2 class="text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 mt-4 mb-2">Evidence checklist (England)</h2>
<p class="text-sm leading-relaxed text-gray-800 mb-2 last:mb-0">Before serving or issuing a claim, make sure you can
produce the following if asked by a court:</p>
<ul class="list-disc pl-5 space-y-1 my-2 text-sm text-gray-800">
<li class="leading-relaxed">A signed AST or clear evidence of the tenancy terms.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Deposit protection certificate and prescribed information service proof.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Current EPC and proof it was given to the tenant.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Gas safety certificates covering the tenancy period.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">How to Rent guide service evidence (if required).</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">A rent schedule showing payments and arrears.</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Proof of notice service (postal receipt, witness statement, or signed acknowledgment).</li>
<li class="leading-relaxed">Any communications relevant to breaches or arrears.</li>
</ul>
